<div id="review_2022524201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2022524201" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2022524201?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2022524201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10513090763337391968">First in the Immortal paranormal fantasy series for Young Adult readers and revolving around Evie Johnson, an unexpectedly gifted student.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>My biggest problem with <em>Immortal</em> is the setting. Shields drops in <em>tells</em> that the school is in England, but my mind kept going to New England as all these girls sound so American! I wish Shields had done a better job of <em>show</em>ing that the story was set in England. Use a more British context in the sentences, British words in the language and Evie’s thought</span>
  <span id="freeText10513090763337391968" style="display:none">First in the Immortal paranormal fantasy series for Young Adult readers and revolving around Evie Johnson, an unexpectedly gifted student.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />My biggest problem with <em>Immortal</em> is the setting. Shields drops in <em>tells</em> that the school is in England, but my mind kept going to New England as all these girls sound so American! I wish Shields had done a better job of <em>show</em>ing that the story was set in England. Use a more British context in the sentences, British words in the language and Evie’s thoughts, and give us a definitive English setting!<br /><br />The theme is power, one which can be used well or badly, and a desire for immortality. <em>I do like Agnes’ approach to it.</em><br /><br />Evie’s introduction to her fellow students made me think of the scene in <em>The Little Princess</em> (an adaptation of a book by Frances Hodgson Burnett) when the news of her father’s death hits home to Shirley Temple’s character, Sarah.<br /><br />I didn’t care for Evie. Sure, her circumstances are sad, but she’s such a shallow twit, and I suspect her perspective with the first-person protagonist point-of-view may be contributing to it. As for Agnes, yes, she has a good heart, but her “escape” to London was stupid and poorly planned. In fact, the whole story’s execution is lame.<br /><br />It is a dramatic soap opera that gets worse as it goes on.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />It begins with a book, <em>The Mysticke Way</em>, brought home by the hungry Sebastian in 1882.<br /><br />It was fate, kismet, that brought Evie Johnson to Sebastian, drawing her into a tangled web of past and present that she cannot control.<br /><br />And as the extraordinary, elemental forces of Wyldcliffe rise up like the mighty sea, Evie is faced with an astounding truth about Sebastian, and her own incredible fate.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Evie Johnson</strong> is sent as a charity girl to a boarding school. <strong>Frances “Frankie” Mary</strong> (born 1933) is Evie’s grandmother who stood in as her mom. <strong>Dad</strong> is a widower posted overseas in the military. <strong>Clara</strong> had been Evie’s mother and Frankie’s daughter.<br /><br /><em>Frankie’s family had…</em><br />…once lived at <strong>Uppercliffe Farm</strong> near Wyldcliffe. Evelyn “<strong>Effie</strong>” Frances Smith was born in 1884 and was Evie’s great-great-grandmother. <strong>Eliza Agnes</strong> was Effie’s daughter born in 1904.<br /><br /><em>The very strict Wyldcliffe Abbey School for Young Ladies is…</em><br />…located in Wyldcliffe (England!). The snotty <strong>Celia Hartle</strong> is High Mistress. <strong>Miss Scratton</strong> is in charge of the girls in the senior division. <strong>Mrs. Edwards</strong> is the housekeeper. <strong>Miss Dalrymple</strong> teaches geography, and the angry <strong>Miss Raglan</strong> teaches math. <strong>Dr. Harrison</strong> is the school doctor. <strong>Miss Schofield</strong> is the sports mistress. <strong>Josh</strong> is a stableboy. <strong>Mr. Brooke</strong> is the music master.<br /><br /><strong>Sarah Fitzalan</strong> is a kind rich girl with a need to rescue. <strong>Bonny</strong> and <strong>Starlight</strong> are her ponies stabled at the school. <strong>Helen Black</strong> is another scholarship student in Evie’s dorm, Cromwell. <strong>Rosie</strong>, <strong>Jessica Armstrong</strong>, <strong>Becky</strong>, <strong>Emily</strong>, <strong>Elizabeth Fisher</strong>, and <strong>Katherine Thomas</strong> are more fellow students. <strong>Celeste</strong> leads the group of mean girls that includes <strong>Sophie</strong> and <strong>India</strong>. <strong>Laura</strong> had been Celeste’s cousin who died.<br /><br /><strong>Dan Jones</strong> runs the store and post office in the village. <strong>Melinda Dawson</strong> is the director of a local museum.<br /><br /><em>Beechwood is…</em><br />…a nursing home. <strong>Margaret Walsh</strong> is one of the nurses.<br /><br /><em>1882</em><br />The sixteen-year-old <strong>Lady Agnes Templeton</strong> has a thirst for knowledge. Her father is <strong>Lord Charles Templeton</strong> who rebuilt Wyldcliffe, using stones from the destroyed abbey. <strong>Miss Binns</strong> is her governess. <strong>Martha</strong> is Agnes’ old nurse who retired to her nephew <strong>John</strong>’s farm. <strong>Nellie</strong> and <strong>Mary</strong> are maids.<br /><br /><strong>S.</strong> is the greedy, immature, and envious young <strong>Sebastian James</strong> — <em>yeah, I don’t care for him, either</em> — who lives at Fairfax Hall. <strong>Sir Edward Fairfax</strong> is his father.<br /><br /><strong>The Reverend A.J. Flowerdew</strong> wrote <em>A Short History of Wyldcliffe Abbey School</em>. <strong>Daniel Jones</strong> was a local carter. <strong>Mr. Carley</strong> is the overseer in London. <strong>Polly</strong> is another of the seamstresses. <strong>Francis Howard</strong> is the consumptive painter Agnes met in London. The <strong>Dark Sisters</strong> are a coven who feed and protect their master.<br /><br />The <strong>Shadow world</strong> is where one is neither alive nor dead.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover is simple and gorgeous in the swirls created by the graceful Talisman drifting down into the water’s depths in a gradation of royal blues ranging from darkest at the top and lightest at the bottom. The title is to the right and just below center is in an embossed gold while the author’s name is at the bottom in black with a small epigram to the left of the pendant in black.<br /><br />The title is what Sebastian wishes to be, <em>Immortal</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10513090763337391968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_142227055" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142227055" />
    <a title="Logan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/980460-logan"><img alt="Logan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558831578p2/980460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142227055?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Logan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Logan" href="/user/show/980460-logan">Logan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/980460-logan?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/980460-logan?shelf=borrowed-ebook">borrowed-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/980460-logan?shelf=own-from-trade">own-from-trade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/980460-logan?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/980460-logan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/980460-logan?shelf=2014-books-read">2014-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142227055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6583810919346758210">For some reason, I don't read very many gothic novels, even though when I <i>do</i> read them I love them. Is it that there aren't many of them written? Are they just not flashy enough to compete with their dystopian brethren? Or do I just not keep them high enough on my radar? This gothic beauty has been languishing on my TBR for a long time, and I'm kicking myself for not getting to it sooner.<br/><br/>Immortal had everything going for it - sweeping romance, eerie moors, haunting ghosts. In the first 100 pages</span>
  <span id="freeText6583810919346758210" style="display:none">For some reason, I don't read very many gothic novels, even though when I <i>do</i> read them I love them. Is it that there aren't many of them written? Are they just not flashy enough to compete with their dystopian brethren? Or do I just not keep them high enough on my radar? This gothic beauty has been languishing on my TBR for a long time, and I'm kicking myself for not getting to it sooner.<br /><br />Immortal had everything going for it - sweeping romance, eerie moors, haunting ghosts. In the first 100 pages, I was enthralled. Evie arrives at Wyldcliffe, only to be nearly run over by a dark, mysterious, and handsome (naturally) boy on a horse. It was a scene ripped from <i>Jane Eyre</i>, that gothic novel to end all gothic novels. I was anticipating the love story to come and finding the secrets hidden in the passageways of the boarding school.<br /><br />Around the midpoint of the book I realized that I needed to adjust my expectations. Evie isn't really haunted so much as she experiences visions. She has odd dreams and keeps seeing a girl who looks like her lurking around the school, but she's never really frightened by any of it. This means, of course, that I was never scared as a reader, either. It took a lot of the fun out of Evie's trips down musty passageways and out onto the moor to meet up with Sebastian.<br /><br />Sebastian, the boy from the horse, runs into her again late one night after Evie has snuck out to get some air. They begin to meet up nightly, and Evie falls in love. I guess. Well, she says she falls in love, but I certainly didn't get swoony over it. This was one romance that just wasn't for me.<br /><br />You see, the book intersperses Evie's story with excerpts from Lady Agnes Templeton's diary from 1882 to 1884. Agnes, the daughter of the owners of Wyldcliffe manor, writes about her friend "S." who introduces her to the Mysticke Way. "S" is kind of a jerk, and as they unlock their mystical powers (witchcraft, though no one in this book wants to call it that), he gets worse.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT! (I think, though it seemed pretty obvious to me.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean, clearly, "S" is Sebastian, right? So I'm reading all about this douche from the past who treated Lady Agnes like complete garbage...and then I'm supposed to be happy that Evie is falling for him? Nope. Not going to happen. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> (Carry on.)<br /><br />The witchcraft bit doesn't really come in to play for Evie's story until late in the book, at which point she has to rush to understand her role in the history of Wyldcliffe much too quickly for my taste.<br /><br />Once Evie finally starts to put together the pieces of the large and obvious clues in front of her, there are only a few chapters left. She has so much to learn and do, which gets rushed into a couple of scenes, only to build to a climax that is resolved so quickly and lacks so much (or any) confrontation that it feels too easy.<br /><br />Instead of wrapping things up with a genuine conflict between Evie and some badass witches in this story, it seems like the author left that for the next in the series. What a letdown! I would have liked to have seen more of Evie developing her own powers and working with her friends. I would have liked to have seen her then use those powers in a manner that actually accomplished something instead of seeming to delay the conflict for a bit.<br /><br />Still, I'm only really complaining because overall I really enjoyed the book. I liked the mystery of Lady Agnes and "S" and how it all tied in with Evie. I loved the setting (boarding school!) and the isolation of this old manor on the moor. I tore through this book - devoured it - to find out what would happen next. It was thoroughly engaging, even if it didn't turn out to be quite the book I wanted it to be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6583810919346758210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132609650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132609650" />
    <a title="Camilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4589066-camilla"><img alt="Camilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372858933p2/4589066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132609650?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camilla" href="/user/show/4589066-camilla">Camilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4589066-camilla?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132609650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17809100793142283590">This was a good read that I sort of enjoyed, I felt that it was lacking certain things that made it disappointing; the characters were okay, the main character, Evie, was likable but a little boring. The whole idea of this book had a lot of potential, the idea of this story is great, but it turned out to be boring at times and a bit predictable. Although, I did like this book because of the cool mystery that ties in with it, and Sebastian's character, to me, made the story interesting and myster</span>
  <span id="freeText17809100793142283590" style="display:none">This was a good read that I sort of enjoyed, I felt that it was lacking certain things that made it disappointing; the characters were okay, the main character, Evie, was likable but a little boring. The whole idea of this book had a lot of potential, the idea of this story is great, but it turned out to be boring at times and a bit predictable. Although, I did like this book because of the cool mystery that ties in with it, and Sebastian's character, to me, made the story interesting and mysterious. The most captivating parts were when him and Evie were together, but that didn't last that long. The beginning was very slow, and I was second guessing if I should even continue reading, but once Sebastian came into the picture and the mystery started to unravel I started to like it. This was an okay read, that I liked, the mystery was cool and the plot was interesting...<br /><br />Evie Johnson is transferring to Wyldcliffe Abbey School as the newest scholarship student, her dad is fighting in the war, her grandmother Frankie is very ill, and her mother died when she was very young. She is torn away from her home, to this Gothic Mansion where only girls attend; it's bleak, expensive, unwelcoming and a life changing experience for Evie. As she heads to the school, a horse runs into her as she is consumed in her thoughts...she falls, opens her eyes, and sees the rider hunched over her. He is a boy, who looks only a few years older than Evie, yet he looks like he comes from another world. His long dark hair frames his pale face, and his blue eyes are staring down at her. Evie finds him very mysterious, and as he rides away he says that they'll meet again, and Evie has a hard time believing that he could be right..but she hopes that he is.<br />Evie enters Wyldcliffe and is welcomed by strict teachers and even stricter rules. She shares a room with Helen, the strange girl who keeps to herself, Celeste, who's snobby, mean, and does whatever she can to make Evie's life difficult, and her two little minions Sophie and Indie. The only friendly face she meets is Sarah, the down to earth, welcoming girl who spends a lot of time with her horses by the stable. Evie tries to meet friends but everyone is shutting her out.<br />She only feels truly happy when she starts to meet the mysterious boy, Sebastian, by the lake at night, he says that this is the only time that he can meet her. Evie spends more time with him and things start to change...Evie starts to see a girl who oddly looks exactly like herself, Helen starts to warn Evie of Sebastian and the meetings by the lake, secrets of the past are revealed, One thing leads to another and the mystery unravels, people aren't what they seem and Evie learns secrets about the school, her family, and Sebastian...<br /><br />I got this book because the description is very promising. The whole idea of this book was great, but I felt it could have been better. I'm split down the middle with this book. The mystery was very cool, and I don't regret reading it. I think I'll read the sequel when it comes out, to see what happens next in the mystery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17809100793142283590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_291625322" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/291625322" />
    <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd"><img alt="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382576238p2/8096484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/291625322?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd">Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of A Great and Terrible Beauty</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd) by: </span>
      The cover
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=harper">harper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=covers-blueness">covers-blueness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=pov-girl">pov-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=school-year-2012-2013">school-year-2012-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=i-give-up">i-give-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=witches-magic-and-more">witches-magic-and-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=hall-of-disappointment-2-or-1-star">hall-of-disappointment-2-or-1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=released-in-2009">released-in-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer291625322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17318414873115294347"><b>
  <u>The Run-Down</u>
</b><br/>Evie Johnson's Grandmother is sick.<br/>And with no other options, Evie gets to become the new scholarship girl at <i>Wyldcliffe Abbey School for Young Ladies</i>.<br/>Turns out that she's filling in the spot for a girl that recently died, there's a mysterious boy, and she keeps seeing a girl that looks very much like her!<br/><i>What is the secret at Wyldcliffe?</i><br/>*dramatic music*<br/><br/><b>
  <u>My Thoughts</u>
</b><br/>This book reminded me much greatly of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3682.A_Great_and_Terrible_Beauty__Gemma_Doyle___1_' title='A Great and Terrible Beauty (Gemma Doyle, #1) by Libba Bray' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Great and Terrible Beauty</a>.<br/>They both involve boarding schools.<br/>They both in</span>
  <span id="freeText17318414873115294347" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>The Run-Down</u>
</b><br />Evie Johnson's Grandmother is sick.<br />And with no other options, Evie gets to become the new scholarship girl at <i>Wyldcliffe Abbey School for Young Ladies</i>.<br />Turns out that she's filling in the spot for a girl that recently died, there's a mysterious boy, and she keeps seeing a girl that looks very much like her!<br /><i>What is the secret at Wyldcliffe?</i><br />*dramatic music*<br /><br /><b>
  <u>My Thoughts</u>
</b><br />This book reminded me much greatly of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3682.A_Great_and_Terrible_Beauty__Gemma_Doyle___1_" title="A Great and Terrible Beauty (Gemma Doyle, #1) by Libba Bray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Great and Terrible Beauty</a>.<br />They both involve boarding schools.<br />They both involve magic.<br />And they both involve girls messing with magic.<br /><br />I wasn't a big fan of <i>A Great and Terrible Beauty</i>.<br />I gave the book 3 stars (which means that I liked it) but I found the characters unlikable.<br />Same thing with this book.<br />I cannot think of a <i>single</i> character that I remotely liked.<br />Most of them I saw as insane, evil, or complete idiots.<br /><br />Evie falls under the idiotic category.<br />There were many things that Evie did that I didn't quite understand <i>why</i> she did them. In all honesty, I can't really elaborate without giving away spoilers.<br /><br />But...<br />I do consider The Romance idiotic.<br />So a mysterious boy almost runs you over with a horse, and of course she falls in love with him!<br /><br />Yeah... The Romance was a major problem for me.<br />Mysterious guy won't tell Evie <i>anything</i> about him, yet she will risk herself to be with him?<br />And <i>where was the romance?</i> What Evie and "Mysterious guy" had was not romance. Its one of those relationships that makes you think <i>"what do they see in each other?"</i> or <i>"What in the world is going on here?"</i><br /><br /><br />Lastly, some parts of the story seemed <i>extremely obvious</i>.<br />There was a diary entries throughout the book from a girl named Lady Agnes. She called a boy in the diary entries S. (even though she called everyone else by name). Do you know who S. could possibly be? (hopefully you do)<br />There were many more obvious things like this and while some of them were obvious thanks to the diary entries, there were others that Evie should have been able to figure out.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>In Conclusion</u>
</b><br />I'm not a huge fan of the book.<br />The characters were unlikable, the romance was stupid, and the story was predictable.<br />If you really <i>really</i> liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3682.A_Great_and_Terrible_Beauty__Gemma_Doyle___1_" title="A Great and Terrible Beauty (Gemma Doyle, #1) by Libba Bray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Great and Terrible Beauty</a> you might like this book. <br />If not? You might want to stay away from this book.<br /><br />I will mention that even though I didn't like this book very much, I will attempt to continue the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17318414873115294347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1116295497" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10452707128740709020">I found the premise of the plot very interesting when I picked it up and thought to myself this seems really good from the sound of it. Half way through I got abit annoyed with the decisions that Evie was constantly making I felt were very carelessly made. But I loved the mystery aspect of the book and what it brought to me entertainment wise. So I feel I was generous with the 2 star rating. <br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>Evie Johnson is transferring to Wyldcliffe Abbey School as the newest scholarship student, her dad is fig</span>
  <span id="freeText10452707128740709020" style="display:none">I found the premise of the plot very interesting when I picked it up and thought to myself this seems really good from the sound of it. Half way through I got abit annoyed with the decisions that Evie was constantly making I felt were very carelessly made. But I loved the mystery aspect of the book and what it brought to me entertainment wise. So I feel I was generous with the 2 star rating. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Evie Johnson is transferring to Wyldcliffe Abbey School as the newest scholarship student, her dad is fighting in the war, her grandmother Frankie is very ill, and her mother died when she was very young. She is torn away from her home, to this Gothic Mansion where only girls attend; it's bleak, expensive, unwelcoming and a life changing experience for Evie. As she heads to the school, a horse runs into her as she is consumed in her thoughts...she falls, opens her eyes, and sees the rider hunched over her. He is a boy, who looks only a few years older than Evie, yet he looks like he comes from another world. His long dark hair frames his pale face, and his blue eyes are staring down at her. Evie finds him very mysterious, and as he rides away he says that they'll meet again, and Evie has a hard time believing that he could be right..but she hopes that he is.<br />Evie enters Wyldcliffe and is welcomed by strict teachers and even stricter rules. She shares a room with Helen, the strange girl who keeps to herself, Celeste, who's snobby, mean, and does whatever she can to make Evie's life difficult, and her two little minions Sophie and Indie. The only friendly face she meets is Sarah, the down to earth, welcoming girl who spends a lot of time with her horses by the stable. Evie tries to meet friends but everyone is shutting her out.<br />She only feels truly happy when she starts to meet the mysterious boy, Sebastian, by the lake at night, he says that this is the only time that he can meet her. Evie spends more time with him and things start to change...Evie starts to see a girl who oddly looks exactly like herself, Helen starts to warn Evie of Sebastian and the meetings by the lake, secrets of the past are revealed, One thing leads to another and the mystery unravels, people aren't what they seem and Evie learns secrets about the school, her family, and Sebastian...<br /><br /><br /><br />The cover is just gorgeous where the story is just plain ok.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xaUw3yKOcuYcDzctEt3TOIVRwsWkhPC/PA34KxJdan+5VD1cBM9jZmwrG5fqNgNX3A7kflHKPyHicwo1BvcGbQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8lFo+HgjQHNsTG6iUfkwjLr/rd0Ra1seUPQW44zoCuuOoGV7XmJR8xxoQhipEuDj46CLZuQllICOiuT9mEJm+Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/145926.Gillian_Shields">About Gillian Shields</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/145926.Gillian_Shields"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1254151589p3/145926.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/145926.Gillian_Shields">Gillian Shields

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8216630831863602674">Gillian Shields was born and brought up in Yorkshire, in the north of England. As she grew up, she had two passions:books and theater. Gillian’s love of books led her to read English at St. Catharine's College, Cambridge. After university she studied acting in London. She then taught in a drama school, the Academy of Live and Recorded Arts, for several years, becoming Vice Principal. She recently </span>
  <span id="freeText8216630831863602674" style="display:none">Gillian Shields was born and brought up in Yorkshire, in the north of England. As she grew up, she had two passions:books and theater. Gillian’s love of books led her to read English at St. Catharine's College, Cambridge. After university she studied acting in London. She then taught in a drama school, the Academy of Live and Recorded Arts, for several years, becoming Vice Principal. She recently taught English and Drama at Beechwood Sacred Heart, a girls’ boarding school.<br /><br />Having children gave Gillian an excuse to carry on reading children’s books, as well as a motivation to write them. She has a son and a daughter, and is married to Brian, who works for the New York Times Media Group.<br /><br /> <br />Hobbies, Interests, and Enthusiasms<br />I am currently learning Italian (or trying to!) and have a secret fantasy about going to live on the beautiful island of Sicily one day, and having a little stone house with a lemon tree in the garden, and a view of the blue, blue sea! I am lucky, though, because I do live in a fantastic part of England, full of soft green fields and rolling hills and cottages that date back four hundred years. <br /><br />I like to go for long walks and see the changes that the seasons bring, and I try to imagine how it all must have been years and years ago, and how the people lived. I was brought up in the north of England which is much more rugged and wild—the backdrop to Immortal. <br /><br />I also enjoy being in the city—although I wouldn't want to live there all the time, it's fun to go window shopping or to big new exhibitions or shows, or just hang out in a coffee shop with a cappuccino and a notebook and watch the busy world go by. <br /><br />Something I enjoy is painting. I have taken quite a few art classes and find it very creative to work with paint and charcoal and images instead of words, though somehow I can't help adding bits of poetry and scraps of words into my paintings, too… When I was at school, I was completely obsessed by the Pre-Raphaelites, and I love the way their art is so intertwined with poetry and stories. My best friend is an artist and she is incredibly inspiring to me.<br /><br />I hate cooking but love the idea of being a good cook and welcoming all my friends and family to delicious meals. So I have lots of beautiful cookery books but I never get past the first couple of recipes. Every so often I get madly enthusiastic all over again, but it doesn't last. <br /><br />When I am writing, I can't listen to music—I find it too distracting, but I love to listen to the radio when I am driving. I listen to pop music in the morning and classical music in the afternoon. That just seems right somehow. My son is really into music, so I enjoy sharing his enthusiasms. At the moment we are listening to Eminem, Akon, NDubz, Chipmunk, Kanye West, plus Greenday, Michael Jackson…the list goes on. My current absolute favorite is Paolo Nutini.<br /><br />Another interest I have is this amazing charity called The Smile Train which carries out operations for disadvantaged children born with harelip/cleft palate. Sometimes I feel I don't realize how lucky I am, and so it's good to try and do something to help a child on the other side of the world who isn't so lucky. My family also tries to support Sightsavers International, who do simple cataract operations to restore the sight of hundreds of people in the developing world.<br /><br />On a more self-indulgent note, I love to get to the theater whenever I can, and to the ballet, which I adore. In another fantasy life I would definitely be a ballerina!<br /><br />I can't imagine getting through a day without reading or writing. I know it sounds a complete cliche, but there it is. I go to a writers' workshop once a week to meet other writers and exchange ideas and read work in progress, and that is hugely important to me. And every spare minute of the time at home I am reading, reading, reading…What would we do without stories? <br />Education<br />St Catharine's College, Cambridge University (MA in Englis</span>

        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
